# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\\n41: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\\n42: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\\n43: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\\n44: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\\n45: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\\n46: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\\n47: //\\n48: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\\n49: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\\n50: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\\n51: // other appropriate content or (2) \\\"absent\\\".\\n52: //\\n53: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\\n54: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\\n55: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\\n56: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\\n57: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\\n58: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\\n59: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\\n60: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\\n61: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\\n62: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\\n63: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\\n64: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\\n65: // selector.\\n66: //\\n67: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\\n68: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\\n69: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\\n73: //\\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\\n75: // during `Run()`.\\n76: //\\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\\n84: //\\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\\n91: //\\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\\n96: // into its constituent parts.\\n97: //\\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\\n100: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\\n101: //\\n102: // A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\\n103: // update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\\n104: // added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\\n105: // stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\\n106: // after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\\n107: // additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\\n108: // client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\\n109: // local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\\n110: // SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\\n111: // update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\\n112: // update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\\n113: // corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\\n114: // and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\\n115: // For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\\n116: // delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\\n117: // object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\\n118: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\\n119: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\\n120: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\\n121: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\\n122: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\\n123: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\\n124: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\\n125: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\\n126: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\\n127: //\\n128: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\\n129: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\\n130: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\\n131: // to something else, for example through a\\n132: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\\n133: //\\n134: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\\n135: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\\n136: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\\n137: type SharedInformer interface {\\n138: \\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\\n139: \\t// the shared informer's resync period. It is like Indexer but does not\\n28: // (necessarily) know how to extract the Store key from a given\\n29: // object.\\n30: //\\n31: // TL;DR caveats: you must not modify anything returned by Get or List as it will break\\n32: // the indexing feature in addition to not being thread safe.\\n33: //\\n34: // The guarantees of thread safety provided by List/Get are only valid if the caller\\n35: // treats returned items as read-only. For example, a pointer inserted in the store\\n36: // through `Add` will be returned as is by `Get`. Multiple clients might invoke `Get`\\n37: // on the same key and modify the pointer in a non-thread-safe way. Also note that\\n38: // modifying objects stored by the indexers (if any) will *not* automatically lead\\n39: // to a re-index. So it's not a good idea to directly modify the objects returned by\\n40: // Get/List, in general.\\n41: type ThreadSafeStore interface {\\n42: \\tAdd(key string, obj interface{})\\n43: \\tUpdate(key string, obj interface{})\\n44: \\tDelete(key string)\\n45: \\tGet(key string) (item interface{}, exists bool)\\n46: \\tList() []interface{}\\n47: \\tListKeys() []string\\n48: \\tReplace(map[string]interface{}, string)\\n49: \\tIndex(indexName string, obj interface{}) ([]interface{}, error)\\n50: \\tIndexKeys(indexName, indexedValue string) ([]string, error)\\n51: \\tListIndexFuncValues(name string) []string\\n52: \\tByIndex(indexName, indexedValue string) ([]interface{}, error)\\n53: \\tGetIndexers() Indexers\\n54: \\n55: \\t// AddIndexers adds more indexers to this store. \"staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go\", \"symbol\": \"HandleDeltas\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Kubernetes SharedInformer factory is a foundational component in client-go that provides efficient, shared caching and watching of Kubernetes API resources. The implementation spans multiple layers:\\n\\n## Factory Layer (Client-Go Informers)\\n\\nThe main entry point is `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/factory.go`, which implements the `SharedInformerFactory` interface. The `sharedInformerFactory` struct manages a collection of `SharedIndexInformer` instances, allowing different informers to share the same underlying cache and watch connections. The factory provides methods:\\n\\n- `NewSharedInformerFactory()` and `NewSharedInformerFactoryWithOptions()` - Factory constructors that accept a Kubernetes client and default resync period\\n- `Start(stopCh)` - Initializes all registered informers in separate goroutines\\n- `WaitForCacheSync(stopCh)` - Blocks until all informer caches have synchronized with the API server\\n- `InformerFor(obj, newFunc)` - Returns or creates a SharedIndexInformer for a given object type\\n\\nThe factory uses `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/internalinterfaces/factory_interfaces.go` to define the core `SharedInformerFactory` interface and `NewInformerFunc` type for creating informers.\\n\\n## Core Informer Infrastructure (Client-Go Cache Tools)\\n\\nThe heart of the SharedInformer implementation is `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go`, which contains:\\n\\n- `SharedInformer` interface - Defines the contract for adding event handlers and managing informer lifecycle\\n- `SharedIndexInformer` interface - Extends SharedInformer with indexing capabilities\\n- `sharedIndexInformer` struct - The main implementation with three core components:\\n  1. An `Indexer` (local cache store with indexing)\\n  2. A `Controller` (coordinates between reflector and processor)\\n  3. A `sharedProcessor` (manages event handler dispatch)\\n\\nWhen `Run()` is called on a SharedIndexInformer, it:\\n1. Creates a `DeltaFIFO` queue (from `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`)\\n2. Constructs a `Config` object that binds the ListerWatcher, queue, and handlers\\n3. Creates a `Controller` to manage the watch/list loop\\n4. Starts the controller and processor goroutines to begin cache synchronization and event distribution\\n\\n## List-Watch Mechanism\\n\\nThe `ListerWatcher` interface in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/listwatch.go` defines two core operations:\\n- `List()` - Fetches all objects matching the selector\\n- `Watch()` - Opens a watch connection for ongoing updates\\n\\nThe `ListWatch` struct provides a convenient implementation, and `NewListWatchFromClient()` creates ListWatchers from REST clients. This enables efficient bidirectional synchronization where the initial list populates the cache and watch events keep it current.\\n\\n## Cache Synchronization Pipeline\\n\\nThe synchronization flow follows this chain:\\n\\n1. **Reflector** (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/reflector.go`) - Watches the API server using the ListerWatcher, calling `List()` initially and then `Watch()` for ongoing changes. It pushes all changes into the DeltaFIFO queue.\\n\\n2. **Controller** (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/controller.go`) - Created with a `Config` containing the DeltaFIFO queue, ListerWatcher, and process function. It runs the reflector and pops items from the queue.\\n\\n3. **DeltaFIFO** (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`) - A special queue that accumulates deltas (add, update, delete operations) for each object. It maintains ordering and allows recovery from watch disconnections.\\n\\n4. **HandleDeltas** - The processor function in SharedIndexInformer that:\\n   - Updates the local `Indexer` cache with each delta\\n   - Sends notifications to all registered event handlers\\n\\n## Storage and Indexing\\n\\n- `Store` interface (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/store.go`) - Basic interface for storing objects\\n- `Indexer` interface (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/index.go`) - Extends Store with indexing capabilities\\n- `ThreadSafeStore` (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go`) - Thread-safe implementation with locking\\n- `FIFO` (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/fifo.go`) - Basic queue implementation\\n\\n## API Server Cache Layer\\n\\nThe API server implements its own caching layer to reduce etcd load:\\n\\n- `Cacher` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go`) - Server-side cache that stores objects in memory\\n- `watchCache` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/watch_cache.go`) - A sliding window cache of watch events\\n- `listerWatcher` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/lister_watcher.go`) - Provides List and Watch from the server-side cache\\n- `cache_watcher` and `watch_cache_interval` - Handle watch streaming with efficient resource version tracking\\n\\nThe Cacher creates a Reflector that continuously syncs from etcd, maintaining the watchCache as a circular buffer of recent events. Clients connecting via watches can replay from the cache if their resource version is recent enough.\\n\\n## Metadata Informer Factory\\n\\nFor dynamic/unstructured access, `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/metadata/metadatainformer/` provides:\\n- `interface.go` - SharedInformerFactory for any GroupVersionResource\\n- `informer.go` - Dynamic informer implementation using unstructured objects\\n\\nThis allows watching any resource type without code generation.\\n\\nThe entire system is designed for efficiency: shared cache connections prevent duplicate watches, DeltaFIFO enables recovery from transient failures, and the multi-layered caching (client-side and server-side) reduces load on etcd while maintaining eventual consistency guarantees across all informer clients.\"\n}\n",

provides efficient, shared caching and watching of Kubernetes API resources. The implementation spans multiple layers:\\n\\n## Factory Layer (Client-Go Informers)\\n\\nThe main entry point is `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/factory.go`, which implements the `SharedInformerFactory` interface. The `sharedInformerFactory` struct manages a collection of `SharedIndexInformer` instances, allowing different informers to share the same underlying cache and watch connections. The factory provides methods:\\n\\n- `NewSharedInformerFactory()` and `NewSharedInformerFactoryWithOptions()` - Factory constructors that accept a Kubernetes client and default resync period\\n- `Start(stopCh)` - Initializes all registered informers in separate goroutines\\n- `WaitForCacheSync(stopCh)` - Blocks until all informer caches have synchronized with the API server\\n- `InformerFor(obj, newFunc)` - Returns or creates a SharedIndexInformer for a given object type\\n\\nThe factory uses `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/internalinterfaces/factory_interfaces.go` to define the core `SharedInformerFactory` interface and `NewInformerFunc` type for creating informers.\\n\\n## Core Informer Infrastructure (Client-Go Cache Tools)\\n\\nThe heart of the SharedInformer implementation is `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go`, which contains:\\n\\n- `SharedInformer` interface - Defines the contract for adding event handlers and managing informer lifecycle\\n- `SharedIndexInformer` interface - Extends SharedInformer with indexing capabilities\\n- `sharedIndexInformer` struct - The main implementation with three core components:\\n  1. An `Indexer` (local cache store with indexing)\\n  2. A `Controller` (coordinates between reflector and processor)\\n  3. A `sharedProcessor` (manages event handler dispatch)\\n\\nWhen `Run()` is called on a SharedIndexInformer, it:\\n1. Creates a `DeltaFIFO` queue (from `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`)\\n2. Constructs a `Config` object that binds the ListerWatcher, queue, and handlers\\n3. Creates a `Controller` to manage the watch/list loop\\n4. Starts the controller and processor goroutines to begin cache synchronization and event distribution\\n\\n## List-Watch Mechanism\\n\\nThe `ListerWatcher` interface in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/listwatch.go` defines two core operations:\\n- `List()` - Fetches all objects matching the selector\\n- `Watch()` - Opens a watch connection for ongoing updates\\n\\nThe `ListWatch` struct provides a convenient implementation, and `NewListWatchFromClient()` creates ListWatchers from REST clients. This enables efficient bidirectional synchronization where the initial list populates the cache and watch events keep it current.\\n\\n## Cache Synchronization Pipeline\\n\\nThe synchronization flow follows this chain:\\n\\n1. **Reflector** (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/reflector.go`) - Watches the API server using the ListerWatcher, calling `List()` initially and then `Watch()` for ongoing changes. It pushes all changes into the DeltaFIFO queue.\\n\\n2. **Controller** (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/controller.go`) - Created with a `Config` containing the DeltaFIFO queue, ListerWatcher, and process function. It runs the reflector and pops items from the queue.\\n\\n3. **DeltaFIFO** (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/delta_fifo.go`) - A special queue that accumulates deltas (add, update, delete operations) for each object. It maintains ordering and allows recovery from watch disconnections.\\n\\n4. **HandleDeltas** - The processor function in SharedIndexInformer that:\\n   - Updates the local `Indexer` cache with each delta\\n   - Sends notifications to all registered event handlers\\n\\n## Storage and Indexing\\n\\n- `Store` interface (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/store.go`) - Basic interface for storing objects\\n- `Indexer` interface (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/index.go`) - Extends Store with indexing capabilities\\n- `ThreadSafeStore` (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go`) - Thread-safe implementation with locking\\n- `FIFO` (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/fifo.go`) - Basic queue implementation\\n\\n## API Server Cache Layer\\n\\nThe API server implements its own caching layer to reduce etcd load:\\n\\n- `Cacher` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/cacher.go`) - Server-side cache that stores objects in memory\\n- `watchCache` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/watch_cache.go`) - A sliding window cache of watch events\\n- `listerWatcher` (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/lister_watcher.go`) - Provides List and Watch from the server-side cache\\n- `cache_watcher` and `watch_cache_interval` - Handle watch streaming with efficient resource version tracking\\n\\nThe Cacher creates a Reflector that continuously syncs from etcd, maintaining the watchCache as a circular buffer of recent events. Clients connecting via watches can replay from the cache if their resource version is recent enough.\\n\\n## Metadata Informer Factory\\n\\nFor dynamic/unstructured access, `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/metadata/metadatainformer/` provides:\\n- `interface.go` - SharedInformerFactory for any GroupVersionResource\\n- `informer.go` - Dynamic informer implementation using unstructured objects\\n\\nThis allows watching any resource type without code generation.\\n\\nThe entire system is designed for efficiency: shared cache connections prevent duplicate watches, DeltaFIFO enables recovery from transient failures, and the multi-layered caching (client-side and server-side) reduces load on etcd while maintaining eventual consistency guarantees across all informer clients.\"\n}\n",
